রুমানা ম্যাম এর সাথে কথা বলেছি। মিড টার্ম আমাদের অনুরধে ১৭ তারিখ নিবে। সিলেবাস হইত আগামি ক্লাস পর্যন্ত যা পরাবে তাই। কিন্তু আমাদের একটা জিনিস মনে রাখতে হবে বা সাক্রিফাইস করতে হবে sampling methodology এর মিড ও কিন্তু বাকি আছে। সো স্যার যদি ১৭ তারিখ নিতে চাই তখন কিন্তু পসিবল না। সেই ক্ষেত্রে আমাদের methodology এর মিড টার্ম হয় ১০ অথবা ২৪ তারিখ দিতে হবে। ২৪ তারিখ স্যার নাও রাজি হতে পারে সো ১০ তারিখেও দেয়ার মানুষিকতা রাখতে হবে। এটা সত্যি যে এক দিনে ২ টা মিড দেয়া কঠিন কিন্তু পাইথন এর সাথে অন্য কোর্স না দেয়াই ভাল। আর ভার্সিটির নিয়ম আছে এক দিনে ২ টা মিড নেয়ার। তাই আমরা প্রয়োজনে প্রয়োজনে থিওরি এক্সাম ২ টা একদিনে দেই।

[30/1/23 02:03:42] Mustain Billah: To become a Data Scientist you need to know :
1. Python, R, Java or any programming language
2. Good Problem-Solving skills using any language which means good knowledge of Data Structure and Algorithms.
3. Good understanding of libraries (numpy, pandas, matplotlib, Tensorflow (Keras) / Pytorch etc.)
4. Structure Query Language(SQL)
5. Statistics, Probability, Mathematics
6. Machine Learning
7. Deep Learning

[16/2/23 22:11:20] ~ Asif: I just put here the of these question answer

1.(i). How could you spot anomalies for each of the variables in the above data set?
As Channel and Region is a nominal level of measurement by using frequency distribution we will able to detect the outlier.
As Fresh, Milk, Grocery, Frozen, Detergents_Paper, Delicassen are ration type, so box plot and/or stem-leaf will detect the outlier.
(ii). Specify the most appropriate measures of central tendency for each of the variables with justification
As Channel, Region are nominal level of measurement hence "Mode" would be appropriate measures of central tendency.
As Fresh, Milk, Grocery, Frozen, Detergents_Paper, Delicassen is ratio type, hence "Mean" would be appropriate measure of central tendency
iii).Find and interpret the maximum and minimum correlations from the following correlation matrix.
Here, the minimum correlation is between "Detergents_Paper" and "Region" -- "-0.001483"
Here, the maxim correlation is in bwteeen "Milk" and "Detergents_Paper" -- "0.661816"
2. Interpret the following pairplots of Milk (Annual spending on milk products), Frozen (Annual spending on frozen products) and Detergents_Paper (Annual spending on detergents and paper products) at Customer’s Channel (‘Blue’ for Channel 1= Hotel/Restaurant/Café; ‘Orange’ for Channel 2= Retail) of Wholesale Customers.
Milk" and "Frozen" has almost no correlation
Milk" and "Detergents_Paper" has Moderate Positive Correlation
Frozen" and "Detergents_Paper" has almost no correlation

[17/2/23 01:14:12] ~ Rahat Bashir: It is generally not appropriate to calculate correlation coefficients between nominal and ratio level data. Correlation coefficients are used to quantify the degree of linear association between two continuous variables that have a meaningful order or scale. Nominal data, on the other hand, consists of categories or groups that do not have a natural order or numeric value associated with them. Therefore, it is not appropriate to calculate correlations between nominal and ratio level data.

[2/3/23 20:37:03] ~ Rushmila: To determine the minimum sample size required to estimate the percent defective within 2% of the true value with 95% confidence level, we can use the following formula:

n = (z^2 * p * q) / E^2

where:

n is the sample size we need
z is the z-score for the desired confidence level (95% confidence level corresponds to a z-score of 1.96)
p is the estimated proportion of defects in the population (we can use 0.5 as a conservative estimate if we don't have any information about the proportion of defects)
q = 1 - p
E is the desired margin of error, which is 2% in this case (0.02)
Plugging in the values we get:

n = (1.96^2 * 0.5 * 0.5) / 0.02^2
n = 9604

Therefore, we need a sample size of at least 9604 to estimate the percent defective within 2% of the true value with 95% confidence level.

[28/3/23 01:27:06] ~ Rasel  Rana: from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X, y, test_size=0.30, random_state=999)

from sklearn.svm import SVC
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report, confusion_matrix, accuracy_score
from sklearn import metrics

SVclf = SVC(kernel='poly', degree=3,probability=True)

SVclf.fit(X_train, y_train)
y_pred=SVclf.predict(X_test)


#=======for the confusion metrix=====
tp, fn, fp, tn = confusion_matrix(y_test, y_pred).ravel()
print("Accuracy Value:", (tp+tn)/(tp+tn+fp+fn))
print("Sensitivity Value:", tp/(tp+fn))
print("Specificity Value:", tn/(tn+fp))
print("Predictive Value Positive:", (tp)/(tp+fp))
print("Predictive Value Negative:", (tn)/(tn+fn))
#end confusion metrix
print('Support Vactor Machine')
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))
print(confusion_matrix(y_test, y_pred))
print(accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred))

#=====create curve=====
y_pred_proba = SVclf.predict_proba(X_test)[::,1]
fpr, tpr, _ = metrics.roc_curve(y_test,  y_pred_proba,pos_label='Good')

plt.plot(fpr,tpr)
plt.plot([0,1],[0,1], color='navy', lw=2, linestyle='--')
plt.xlim([0.0, 1.0])
plt.ylim([0.0, 1.05])
plt.ylabel('True Positive Rate')
plt.xlabel('False Positive Rate')
plt.show()

[30/3/23 20:57:07] ~ Rahat Bashir: # Draw the ROC curve

# Calculate the probability of the predicted values
y_pred_prob = SVclassifier.predict_proba(X_test)[:,1]


# Calculate the false positive rate (FPR), true positive rate (TPR) at various thresholds
fpr, tpr, thresholds = roc_curve(y_test, y_pred_prob, pos_label='Low')
auc_score = roc_auc_score(y_test, y_pred_prob, multi_class='ovr')


# Calculate the area under the ROC curve (AUC)
roc_auc = auc(fpr, tpr)


# Plot the ROC curve
plt.plot(fpr, tpr, color='magenta', lw=1, label='ROC curve (area = %0.2f)'% roc_auc)
plt.plot([0,1],[0,1], color='navy', lw=1, linestyle='dotted')
plt.xlim([0.0, 1.0])
plt.ylim([0.0, 1.05])
plt.xlabel('False Positive Rate')
plt.ylabel('True Positive Rate')
plt.title('ROC Curve (AUC = {:.2f}) SVM'.format(auc_score))
plt.legend(loc='center right')
plt.show()
plt.close()

কেন SKS tower সিলেক্ট করা হল ?
১) cool environment
2) Prayer & ablution facilities
3) center location in the city ( available transport )
যে কোন এরিয়া থেকে sks tower এ আসতে সুবিধা হবে. কারো লোকেশন চিনতে প্রবলেম হলে আমাকে ইনবক্স করবেন আমি বলে দিব কিভাবে সহজ ভাবে আসতে পারবেন।
ইফতার মেনু ঃ গতকালকের দেয়া মেনু অনুযায়ী সেট ০২ ও ০৩ ২ টাই সিলেক্ট করা হয়েছে । যার যেটা খুশি সেটা সিলেক্ট করতে পারবেন।
মেনু ০২ - ৩২০ টাকা
মেনু ০৩ - ২৭০ টাকা
(সাথে জুস থাকবে।)
কনফার্মেশন ঃ ইফতার মেনু কত জনের জন্য হবে সেটা কাল দুপুর ১২ টার ভিতর জানাতে হবে। সো আপনারা কাল ১২ টার ভিতর আমাকে কনফার্ম করেন। যত জন হবে তত জনকে নিয়েই ইফতার হবে।
(চেষ্টা করবেন অংশগ্রহন করতে)
তাই শেষ সময়ের জন্য অপেক্ষা না করে দ্রুত জানান।
বিকাশ ঃ 01912470915 ( পার্সোনাল )
কেউ যদি এসে টাকা দিতে চান সেক্ষেত্রে আমাকে ইনবক্স এ কনফার্ম করেন। তবে কনফার্ম করলে অফ কোর্স আসতে হবে। কারন আমি যত জনের জন্য অর্ডার করবো সেটা কনফার্ম বিল দিতে হবে।

[20/5/23 22:59:15] Mustain Billah: What is Cross Validation?
Cross Validation is a process of building a machine learning model which ensures that models train correctly.

Example: You are a student. In your book, there are twelve chapters, and your teacher told you that questions will come from six chapters. But in the exam, questions come from ten chapters. So you couldn't do well in the exam. Now, if anyone judges you as a weak student, then it will be incorrect judgement.
In another case, your teacher told you that questions will come from all the chapters, but in the exam, only six questions come from six chapters. Even if you did well in the exam, it wouldn't be the perfect evaluation.

Above two cases, you were not evaluated properly.

In order to perfectly test you, questions should come from all the chapters.

So, in the case of model training, cross-validation ensure that model fits perfectly.

Types of Cross-validation:
1. K-fold Cross-validation 
2. Stratified k-fold Cross-validation
3. Group k-fold Cross-validation
4. Hold-out based validation
5. Group k-fold Cross-validation

Code Link: https://github.com/mddmustainbillah/Machine_learning_AT/blob/main/Different%20max_depth%20ploting%20and%20Cross%20Validation.ipynb

Assignment এর জন্য ম্যাম আমাদের কাছে ডেট চেয়েছে । 
আমি মনে করি জুলাই এর ২৮ তারিখ নেয়া উচিত রাজি না হলে ২১ তারিখ। 
ম্যাম ঈদ এর পর ১ম ক্লাস এ মিড টার্ম নিতে চেয়েছিলেন , আমি মনে করি ৭ জুলাই ক্লাস শুরু হলে দিয়ে দেয়া উচিত আর সাথে একটা কুইজ নিবে, তবে ঐ দিন মাল্টিভ্যারিয়াট মিড টার্ম ও আছে ও Assignment জমা দিতে হবে। 
মাল্টিভ্যারিয়াট লজিকাল ফাংশন আর রিসার্চ বুঝে পড়েই ভালো এক্সাম দেয়া যাবে। কিন্তু এখন যদি রিসার্চ পিছাই তাহলে Machine learning and Inference এর সাথে conflict হয়ে যাবে এবং আরও কঠিন হয়ে যাবে। 
তাই আমার মতামত ঈদ ছুটি কাজে লাগিয়ে, ঈদ এর পর ১ম ক্লাস এ ২ টা মিড একি দিনে দিয়ে , বাকি ২ টা মিড আলাদা দিনে দেয়ার চেষ্টা করি।

[7/7/23 14:51:00] ~ Asif: Backpropagation is a method of training artificial neural networks. It works by computing the gradient of the loss function with respect to all the weights in the network, and then using this gradient to update the weights in a way that minimizes the loss.

The backpropagation algorithm works in three steps:

Forward pass: The network is first fed with a set of inputs. The inputs are then propagated through the network, layer by layer, until they reach the output layer. At each layer, the activation of each neuron is calculated based on the activations of the neurons in the previous layer and the weights between them.
Backward pass: The error between the network's output and the desired output is then propagated back through the network, layer by layer. This is done by calculating the derivative of the loss function with respect to the activation of each neuron. The derivatives are then multiplied by the weights between the neurons, and the results are added to the weights. This process is repeated for each layer in the network.
Weight update: Once the backward pass is complete, the weights in the network are updated using a gradient descent algorithm. The gradient descent algorithm updates the weights in the direction that minimizes the loss function.
The backpropagation algorithm is repeated for a number of iterations, or epochs. After each epoch, the weights in the network are updated, and the network is then fed with a new set of inputs. This process continues until the network converges, meaning that the loss function is no longer decreasing.

Backpropagation is a powerful method for training artificial neural networks. It is relatively simple to implement, and it can be used to train networks of any size. However, backpropagation can be computationally expensive, especially for large networks.

Here are some of the advantages of backpropagation:

It is a simple and efficient method for training artificial neural networks.
It can be used to train networks of any size.
It is relatively robust to noise and outliers in the training data.
Here are some of the disadvantages of backpropagation:

It can be computationally expensive, especially for large networks.
It can be difficult to tune the hyperparameters of the backpropagation algorithm, such as the learning rate.
Backpropagation can sometimes get stuck in local minima, meaning that the network does not converge to the optimal solution.

[14/7/23 15:34:19] ~ Tonmoy: Based on the provided output, we can classify the tuple X-(Class-2nd, Sex-*, Age-Adult) using the Naive Bayes classifier.

First, let's look at the conditional probabilities for each attribute:

For the Class attribute:

P(Class=2nd|Survived=No) = 0.11208054
P(Class=2nd|Survived=Yes) = 0.16596343
For the Sex attribute:

P(Sex=Male|Survived=No) = 0.91543624
P(Sex=Male|Survived=Yes) = 0.51617440
For the Age attribute:

P(Age=Adult|Survived=No) = 0.96510067
P(Age=Adult|Survived=Yes) = 0.91983122
To classify the tuple X-(Class-2nd, Sex-*, Age-Adult), we need to calculate the posterior probabilities for each class label:

P(Survived=No|Class=2nd, Sex=*, Age=Adult) ∝ P(Survived=No) * P(Class=2nd|Survived=No) * P(Sex=Male|Survived=No) * P(Age=Adult|Survived=No)
P(Survived=Yes|Class=2nd, Sex=*, Age=Adult) ∝ P(Survived=Yes) * P(Class=2nd|Survived=Yes) * P(Sex=Male|Survived=Yes) * P(Age=Adult|Survived=Yes)
Let's calculate the probabilities:

P(Survived=No|Class=2nd, Sex=, Age=Adult) = 0.676965 * 0.11208054 * 0.91543624 * 0.96510067 P(Survived=Yes|Class=2nd, Sex=, Age=Adult) = 0.323035 * 0.16596343 * 0.51617440 * 0.91983122

Comparing the two probabilities, we can see that P(Survived=No|Class=2nd, Sex=*, Age=Adult) is higher.

Therefore, the tuple X-(Class-2nd, Sex-*, Age-Adult) is classified as "Survived=No" based on the Naive Bayes classification.
[14/7/23 15:43:36] ~ Tonmoy: Information Gain, Gain Ratio, and Gini Index are commonly used measures for attribute selection in classification and regression tree models. These measures help determine the most informative attributes for splitting the data and building decision trees.

1. Information Gain: Information Gain is a measure of the reduction in entropy (uncertainty) achieved by splitting the data based on a particular attribute. It quantifies how much information is gained by knowing the value of an attribute for predicting the class label. Higher Information Gain indicates that the attribute provides more useful information for classification.

2. Gain Ratio: Gain Ratio is an enhancement of Information Gain that takes into account the intrinsic information of each attribute. It addresses the bias towards attributes with a large number of distinct values by normalizing the Information Gain with the Split Information. Gain Ratio reduces the bias and helps in selecting attributes that are more balanced and informative.

3. Gini Index: Gini Index measures the impurity or disorder of a set of class labels in a given dataset. It represents the probability of incorrectly classifying a randomly chosen element in the dataset. Lower Gini Index indicates a higher level of purity and better attribute for classification. Gini Index is calculated as the sum of squared probabilities of each class label subtracted from 1.

Now, let's analyze the given values of Gini Index for attributes X, Y, Z, and W:
- Gini(D) = 0.48 (attribute X)
- Gini(D) = 0.44 (attribute Y)
- Gini(D) = 0.36 (attribute Z)
- Gini(D) = 0.38 (attribute W)

The attribute with the lowest Gini Index is attribute Z, which has a Gini(D) value of 0.36. Since the Gini Index measures impurity, the attribute with the lowest value indicates the attribute that provides the most pure splits and contributes the most to the separation of classes. Therefore, attribute Z should be selected for the split as it would result in the best separation of classes and the highest purity in the resulting subsets.

[8/8/23 16:13:50] ~ Asif: Data Scientist

Job Description
• Deliver Data Analytic & AI related and innovative projects in the digital, social, and big data space.
• Extracting, manipulating and analyzing different datasets (like social, search, PRM) to obtain business insights.
• Generating business insights to support senior leadership decision making.
• Storyboarding and creation of final outputs
• Devising and advising on options for new analytics techniques and methods
• Working with advanced tools, such as natural language processors, visualization tools etc, where some domain knowledge is required and/or programming skills are necessary.
• Build fundamental statistical/econometric/machine learning models for service delivery, according to the definitions and designs of the Signature Projects Manager
• Create Python/R based tools to obtain advanced business insights.
• Build queries and conduct analysis to fulfill advanced business requests.

Requirements
1- Bachelor’s degree in information technologies or relevant education
2- Experience from 1-3 Years.
3- AWS Certified.

Please, send your CVs to careers@pinpoint-hr.com

[29/9/23 16:04:32] ~ Rasel  Rana: data snoring;
input snoring disease total;
datalines;
0 24 1379
2 35 638
4 21 213
5 30 254
;

proc genmod data=snoring;
model disease/total=snoring/dist=binomial link==identity;
proc genmod data=snoring;
model disease/total=snoring/dist=binomial link=logit;
proc genmod data=snoring;
model disease/total=snoring/dist=binomial link==probit;
run;
